> Yes, propose a plan for all your items from 1 to 5, and consider this: 1. Enhance Parsons Problem FeedbackThe current feedback for incorrect sequences

is minimal. Simply showing the correct answer isn't enough for learning.Recommendation: Implement a "diff" view for the user's incorrect answer against

the correct one.â€¢Visual Cues: Show the user's sequence. Underneath, show the correct sequence. Use colors to highlight correct, incorrect, and
out-of-place blocks.â€¢Green: Correct block in the correct position.â€¢Yellow/Orange: Correct block in the wrong position.â€¢Red: An extraneous or incorrect

block (if applicable).â€¢Explain the "Why": For key steps that are out of order, provide a brief explanation. For example, if service password-encryption is

 placed before password cisco, the explanation could be: "The service password-encryption command only encrypts plaintext passwords already in the
configuration. It should be run after setting the console and VTY passwords."2. Improve Feedback for Binary (T/F) QuestionsThe message "No retry for
binary questions" is a dead end for the learner. The goal is to correct misconceptions immediately.Recommendation: When a user answers a T/F question

incorrectly, provide an immediate, concise explanation.â€¢Example (from the log):â€¢Question: "ARP messages are encapsulated within an IPv4 header."â€¢User

Answer: Trueâ€¢Improved Feedback: "âœ— Incorrect. The correct answer is False. ARP operates at Layer 2 (the Data Link Layer) to find a MAC address from an IP

address. Because it stays within the local network, its messages are encapsulated in Ethernet frames, not IP packets."3. Fulfill the "Diagnosis"
PromiseThe application diagnoses FATIGUE_ERROR or DISCRIMINATION_ERROR and promises a "side-by-side comparison," but this never materializes. This is a

critical UX gap.Recommendation: Actually create and display the comparison.â€¢When Triggered: After diagnosing the error, present a clear, two-column view

comparing the concepts the user is confusing.â€¢Example (from the log): The user confused ARP's direction.â€¢Comparison View: | ARP (Address Resolution
Protocol) | Reverse ARP (RARP) / DHCP | | :--- | :--- | | Resolves: IP Address â†’ MAC Address | Resolves: MAC Address â†’ IP Address | | Question: "What is

the MAC address for 192.168.1.10?" | Question: "I'm MAC address AABB.CC00.1122. What's my IP?" | | Analogy: Finding a house number (MAC) when you know the

 person's name (IP). | Analogy: A new employee asking for their assigned computer name (IP). |4. Refine the Socratic Dialogue ("Let's Think Together")The

dialogue on the /26 subnet mask was a great idea but faltered. The user was on the right track, but the system seemed to misinterpret their input and

ended the dialogue abruptly.Recommendation:â€¢Better Intent Recognition: Improve the NLP or pattern matching to better understand the user's free-form text.

 The user correctly identified the binary 11000000, which should have been recognized as a major step forward.â€¢Graceful Closure: Even if the user doesn't

get the final answer, the dialogue should conclude by connecting their correct steps to the final solution.â€¢Example: "You were exactly right that the

binary is 11000000! The final step is to convert that to decimal. The first '1' is the 128's place and the second is the 64's place. Adding them together

(128 + 64) gives us 192. Well done getting the binary part right!"5. Address Content/Tooling BugsThe MCQ where the user correctly answered "all hosts in

the same subnet" but was marked wrong is a trust-killer.Recommendation:â€¢Implement a Flagging System: Allow users to flag a question they think is
incorrect. This provides valuable data for content review.â€¢Rigorous Content Review: The question bank needs to be periodically reviewed for accuracy,

especially for subtle distinctions like "subnet" vs. "network."By implementing these changes, cortex can evolve from a good quiz tool into a truly
adaptive and effective learning partner that not only tests knowledge but actively builds it.

     NEAR_CORRECT_PATTERNS = [

     New Migration: src/db/migrations/022_user_flags.sql

     CREATE TABLE user_flags (

         id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

         atom_id UUID REFERENCES learning_atoms(id),

         user_id TEXT,  -- Future: actual user system

         flag_type TEXT NOT NULL,  -- 'wrong_answer', 'ambiguous', 'typo', 'outdated'

         flag_reason TEXT,

         created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT NOW(),

         resolved_at TIMESTAMP,

         resolution_notes TEXT

     );


     CREATE INDEX idx_user_flags_atom ON user_flags(atom_id);

     CREATE INDEX idx_user_flags_unresolved ON user_flags(resolved_at) WHERE resolved_at IS NULL;

     Add check for correct: null:

     def check_mcq_correct_index(row) -> tuple[bool, str]:

         """Ensure MCQ has valid correct_index (not null)."""

         back = json.loads(row.back) if row.back else {}

         if back.get("correct") is None and back.get("correct_index") is None:

             return False, "MCQ missing correct answer index"

         return True, ""

      782 +def render_tf_feedback_panel(

      783 +    console: Console,

      784 +    correct: bool,

      785 +    correct_answer: str,

      786 +    user_answer: str,

      787 +    explanation: str | None = None,

      788 +) -> None:

      789 +    """

      790 +    Render educational feedback for True/False questions.

      791 +

      792 +    Unlike generic result panels, this provides specific educational context

      793 +    for binary questions where retry isn't allowed.

      794 +

      795 +    Args:

      796 +        console: Rich Console instance

      797 +        correct: Whether user's answer was correct

      798 +        correct_answer: The correct answer (True/False)

      799 +        user_answer: What the user answered

      800 +        explanation: Why the statement is true/false

      801 +    """

      802 +    color = CORTEX_THEME["success"] if correct else CORTEX_THEME["error"]

      803 +    icon = "â—‰" if correct else "âœ—"

      804 +    status = "CORRECT" if correct else "INCORRECT"

      805 +

      806 +    content = Text()

      807 +    content.append(f"{icon} {status}\n\n", style=Style(color=color, bold=True))

      808 +

      809 +    # Show answer comparison for wrong answers

      810 +    if not correct:

      811 +        content.append("You answered: ", style=STYLES["cortex_dim"])

      812 +        content.append(f"{user_answer}\n", style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["error"]))

      813 +        content.append("Correct answer: ", style=STYLES["cortex_dim"])

      814 +        content.append(f"{correct_answer}\n\n", style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["success"], bold=True))

      815 +

      816 +    # Educational explanation - the key learning value

      817 +    if explanation:

      818 +        content.append("â”€" * 40 + "\n", style=STYLES["cortex_dim"])

      819 +        content.append("WHY: ", style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["warning"], bold=True))

      820 +        content.append(explanation, style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["white"]))

      821 +    else:

      822 +        # Fallback if no explanation available

      823 +        content.append("â”€" * 40 + "\n", style=STYLES["cortex_dim"])

      824 +        content.append(

      825 +            f"The statement is {correct_answer.upper()} - review this concept.",

      826 +            style=STYLES["cortex_dim"],

      827 +        )

      828 +

      829 +    console.print(Panel(

      830 +        content,

      831 +        title="[bold]TRUE/FALSE FEEDBACK[/bold]",

      832 +        border_style=Style(color=color),

      833 +        box=box.HEAVY,

      834 +        padding=(1, 2),

      835 +    ))

      836 +

      837 +

      838  # =============================================================================

      839  # ASI-STYLE PROMPTS

      840  # =============================================================================

       65      return True, ""

       66

       67

       68 +def check_mcq_back_correct(atom_type: str, back: str | None) -> tuple[bool, str]:

       69 +    """

       70 +    Check if MCQ back field JSON has valid 'correct' value.

       71 +

       72 +    Some MCQs store correct answer as JSON in back field:

       73 +    {"options": [...], "correct": 0}

       74 +

       75 +    If correct is null/None, the question has no valid answer.

       76 +    """

       77 +    if atom_type != "mcq":

       78 +        return True, ""

       79 +

       80 +    if not back:

       81 +        return True, ""  # Will be caught by null content check

       82 +

       83 +    back_str = str(back).strip()

       84 +    if not back_str.startswith("{"):

       85 +        return True, ""  # Not JSON format, skip

       86 +

       87 +    try:

       88 +        data = json.loads(back_str)

       89 +    except json.JSONDecodeError:

       90 +        return True, ""  # JSON errors caught elsewhere

       91 +

       92 +    if not isinstance(data, dict):

       93 +        return True, ""

       94 +

       95 +    # Check if 'correct' key exists and is null

       96 +    if "correct" in data and data["correct"] is None:

       97 +        return False, "MCQ back JSON has 'correct: null' - no valid answer"

       98 +

       99 +    # Check if correct is out of bounds

      100 +    options = data.get("options", [])

      101 +    correct = data.get("correct")

      102 +    if correct is not None and isinstance(correct, int):

      103 +        if correct < 0 or (options and correct >= len(options)):

      104 +            return False, f"MCQ back JSON 'correct: {correct}' out of bounds"

      105 +

      106 +    return True, ""

      107 +

      108 +

      109  def check_source_refs(content_json: dict | None, source_fact_basis: str | None) -> bool:

      110      """Check if atom has valid source traceability."""

      111      # Check content_json for source_refs

      838 +def render_parsons_diff_panel(

      839 +    console: Console,

      840 +    user_sequence: list[str],

      841 +    correct_sequence: list[str],

      842 +    step_explanations: dict[int, str] | None = None,

      843 +) -> None:

      844 +    """

      845 +    Render enhanced side-by-side diff for Parsons problems.

      846 +

      847 +    Shows:

      848 +    - Left column: User's sequence with status icons

      849 +    - Right column: Correct sequence

      850 +    - Color coding: âœ“ green (correct position), ~ yellow (wrong position), âœ— red (extra)

      851 +    - Optional step explanations for key ordering reasons

      852 +

      853 +    Args:

      854 +        console: Rich Console instance

      855 +        user_sequence: List of steps in user's order

      856 +        correct_sequence: List of steps in correct order

      857 +        step_explanations: Optional dict mapping step index to explanation why order matters

      858 +    """

      859 +    from rich.table import Table

      860 +

      861 +    # Build comparison table

      862 +    table = Table(

      863 +        box=box.DOUBLE_EDGE,

      864 +        border_style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["error"]),

      865 +        show_header=True,

      866 +        header_style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["primary"], bold=True),

      867 +    )

      868 +    table.add_column("#", width=3, justify="center")

      869 +    table.add_column("Your Sequence", ratio=2, overflow="fold")

      870 +    table.add_column("", width=3, justify="center")  # Status

      871 +    table.add_column("Correct Sequence", ratio=2, overflow="fold")

      872 +

      873 +    correct_set = set(correct_sequence)

      874 +    max_len = max(len(user_sequence), len(correct_sequence))

      875 +

      876 +    for i in range(max_len):

      877 +        step_num = str(i + 1)

      878 +        user_step = user_sequence[i] if i < len(user_sequence) else ""

      879 +        correct_step = correct_sequence[i] if i < len(correct_sequence) else ""

      880 +

      881 +        # Determine status

      882 +        if user_step == correct_step:

      883 +            icon = "âœ“"

      884 +            user_style = Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["success"])

      885 +            correct_style = Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["success"])

      886 +        elif user_step in correct_set:

      887 +            icon = "~"

      888 +            user_style = Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["warning"])

      889 +            correct_style = Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["dim"])

      890 +        elif user_step:

      891 +            icon = "âœ—"

      892 +            user_style = Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["error"])

      893 +            correct_style = Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["dim"])

      894 +        else:

      895 +            icon = "â—‹"

      896 +            user_style = Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["dim"])

      897 +            correct_style = Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["warning"])

      898 +

      899 +        table.add_row(

      900 +            Text(step_num, style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["dim"])),

      901 +            Text(user_step, style=user_style),

      902 +            Text(icon, style=user_style),

      903 +            Text(correct_step, style=correct_style),

      904 +        )

      905 +

      906 +    # Legend

      907 +    legend = Text()

      908 +    legend.append("âœ“ ", style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["success"]))

      909 +    legend.append("Correct  ", style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["dim"]))

      910 +    legend.append("~ ", style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["warning"]))

      911 +    legend.append("Wrong position  ", style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["dim"]))

      912 +    legend.append("âœ— ", style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["error"]))

      913 +    legend.append("Missing/Extra", style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["dim"]))

      914 +

      915 +    content = Text()

      916 +    content.append_text(legend)

      917 +    content.append("\n\n")

      918 +

      919 +    # Show step explanations if provided

      920 +    if step_explanations:

      921 +        content.append("â”€" * 50 + "\n", style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["dim"]))

      922 +        content.append("WHY ORDER MATTERS:\n", style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["warning"], bold=True))

      923 +        for idx, explanation in step_explanations.items():

      924 +            if idx < len(correct_sequence):

      925 +                content.append(f"  Step {idx + 1}: ", style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["primary"]))

      926 +                content.append(f"{explanation}\n", style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["white"]))

      927 +

      928 +    console.print(Panel(

      929 +        Columns([table], padding=(1, 2)),

      930 +        title="[bold]SEQUENCE COMPARISON[/bold]",

      931 +        border_style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["error"]),

      932 +        box=box.HEAVY,

      933 +    ))

      934 +

      935 +    if step_explanations:

      936 +        console.print(Panel(

      937 +            content,

      938 +            border_style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["warning"]),

      939 +            box=box.ROUNDED,

      940 +        ))

      941 +

      942 +

      943  # =============================================================================

      944  # ASI-STYLE PROMPTS

      945  # =============================================================================

       943 +def prompt_flag_option(console: Console) -> str | None:

       944 +    """

       945 +    Prompt user to flag a problematic question after incorrect answer.

       946 +

       947 +    Shows a subtle prompt that doesn't interrupt flow but allows reporting.

       948 +

       949 +    Returns:

       950 +        flag_type if user chose to flag, None otherwise

       951 +    """

       952 +    from rich.prompt import Prompt

       953 +

       954 +    console.print(

       955 +        "\n[dim]Think this question has an issue? "

       956 +        "Press [bold]f[/bold] to flag, [bold]Enter[/bold] to continue[/dim]"

       957 +    )

       958 +

       959 +    response = Prompt.ask(

       960 +        "[dim]>[/dim]",

       961 +        default="",

       962 +        show_default=False,

       963 +    ).strip().lower()

       964 +

       965 +    if response != "f":

       966 +        return None

       967 +

       968 +    # Show flag type options

       969 +    console.print("\n[bold cyan]FLAG TYPE[/bold cyan]")

       970 +    console.print("  [cyan]1[/cyan] - Wrong answer (correct answer is incorrect)")

       971 +    console.print("  [cyan]2[/cyan] - Ambiguous (question unclear)")

       972 +    console.print("  [cyan]3[/cyan] - Typo (spelling/grammar)")

       973 +    console.print("  [cyan]4[/cyan] - Outdated (info no longer accurate)")

       974 +    console.print("  [cyan]5[/cyan] - Other")

       975 +    console.print("  [dim]c[/dim] - Cancel")

       976 +

       977 +    flag_choice = Prompt.ask(

       978 +        ">_ [cyan]SELECT[/cyan]",

       979 +        choices=["1", "2", "3", "4", "5", "c"],

       980 +        default="c",

       981 +    )

       982 +

       983 +    flag_types = {

       984 +        "1": "wrong_answer",

       985 +        "2": "ambiguous",

       986 +        "3": "typo",

       987 +        "4": "outdated",

       988 +        "5": "other",

       989 +    }

       990 +

       991 +    flag_type = flag_types.get(flag_choice)

       992 +

       993 +    if flag_type:

       994 +        # Optional reason

       995 +        reason = Prompt.ask(

       996 +            "[dim]Reason (optional, press Enter to skip)[/dim]",

       997 +            default="",

       998 +        ).strip()

       999 +

      1000 +        console.print(

      1001 +            f"[green]Flag recorded:[/green] {flag_type}"

      1002 +            + (f" - {reason}" if reason else "")

      1003 +        )

      1004 +        return {"type": flag_type, "reason": reason} if reason else {"type": flag_type}

      1005 +

      1006 +    return None

      1007 +

      1008 +

      1009  # =============================================================================

      1010  # ASI-STYLE PROMPTS

      1011  # =============================================================================

      600 +    def _record_flag(self, note: dict, flag_data: dict) -> None:

      601 +        """Record a user flag for a problematic question."""

      602 +        atom_id = note.get("id")

      603 +        if not atom_id or not flag_data:

      604 +            return

      605 +

      606 +        try:

      607 +            from sqlalchemy import text

      608 +            from src.db.database import get_session

      609 +

      610 +            with next(get_session()) as session:

      611 +                # Try to insert flag, ignore if table doesn't exist yet

      612 +                session.execute(

      613 +                    text("""

      614 +                        INSERT INTO user_flags (atom_id, flag_type, flag_reason, session_id)

      615 +                        VALUES (:atom_id, :flag_type, :flag_reason, :session_id)

      616 +                    """),

      617 +                    {

      618 +                        "atom_id": str(atom_id),

      619 +                        "flag_type": flag_data.get("type", "other"),

      620 +                        "flag_reason": flag_data.get("reason"),

      621 +                        "session_id": str(self.session_id) if hasattr(self, "session_id") else None,

      622 +                    }

      623 +                )

      624 +                session.commit()

      625 +                logger.info(f"Recorded flag for atom {atom_id}: {flag_data.get('type')}")

      626 +        except Exception as e:

      627 +            # Silently fail if table doesn't exist - migration may not have run

      628 +            logger.debug(f"Could not record flag (table may not exist): {e}")

      1009 +def render_contrastive_panel(

      1010 +    console: Console,

      1011 +    concept_a: dict,

      1012 +    concept_b: dict,

      1013 +    confusion_evidence: str | None = None,

      1014 +) -> None:

      1015 +    """

      1016 +    Render side-by-side concept comparison for discrimination errors.

      1017 +

      1018 +    When learners confuse similar concepts, this panel shows them

      1019 +    side-by-side with key differentiating facts highlighted.

      1020 +

      1021 +    Args:

      1022 +        console: Rich Console instance

      1023 +        concept_a: Dict with 'name', 'definition', 'key_facts' (list), 'example'

      1024 +        concept_b: Dict with same structure

      1025 +        confusion_evidence: Optional string explaining why learner confused them

      1026 +    """

      1027 +    from rich.table import Table

      1028 +

      1029 +    # Build comparison table

      1030 +    table = Table(

      1031 +        box=box.DOUBLE_EDGE,

      1032 +        border_style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["primary"]),

      1033 +        show_header=True,

      1034 +        header_style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["primary"], bold=True),

      1035 +        title="[bold]CONCEPT COMPARISON[/bold]",

      1036 +        title_style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["warning"], bold=True),

      1037 +    )

      1038 +

      1039 +    name_a = concept_a.get("name", "Concept A")

      1040 +    name_b = concept_b.get("name", "Concept B")

      1041 +

      1042 +    table.add_column(name_a, ratio=1, style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["accent"]))

      1043 +    table.add_column(name_b, ratio=1, style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["secondary"]))

      1044 +

      1045 +    # Definition row

      1046 +    def_a = concept_a.get("definition", "")

      1047 +    def_b = concept_b.get("definition", "")

      1048 +    table.add_row(

      1049 +        Text(def_a, style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["white"])),

      1050 +        Text(def_b, style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["white"])),

      1051 +    )

      1052 +

      1053 +    # Key facts rows

      1054 +    facts_a = concept_a.get("key_facts", [])

      1055 +    facts_b = concept_b.get("key_facts", [])

      1056 +    max_facts = max(len(facts_a), len(facts_b))

      1057 +

      1058 +    for i in range(max_facts):

      1059 +        fact_a = facts_a[i] if i < len(facts_a) else ""

      1060 +        fact_b = facts_b[i] if i < len(facts_b) else ""

      1061 +        table.add_row(

      1062 +            Text(f"â€¢ {fact_a}", style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["dim"])) if fact_a else Text(""),

      1063 +            Text(f"â€¢ {fact_b}", style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["dim"])) if fact_b else Text(""),

      1064 +        )

      1065 +

      1066 +    # Example row (highlighted)

      1067 +    example_a = concept_a.get("example", "")

      1068 +    example_b = concept_b.get("example", "")

      1069 +    if example_a or example_b:

      1070 +        table.add_row(

      1071 +            Text(f"Ex: {example_a}", style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["success"], italic=True)) if example_a else Text(""),

      1072 +            Text(f"Ex: {example_b}", style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["success"], italic=True)) if example_b else Text(""),

      1073 +        )

      1074 +

      1075 +    console.print(Panel(

      1076 +        table,

      1077 +        border_style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["warning"]),

      1078 +        box=box.HEAVY,

      1079 +        padding=(1, 2),

      1080 +    ))

      1081 +

      1082 +    # Show confusion evidence if available

      1083 +    if confusion_evidence:

      1084 +        console.print(Panel(

      1085 +            Text.assemble(

      1086 +                ("WHY YOU MIGHT CONFUSE THEM: ", Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["warning"], bold=True)),

      1087 +                (confusion_evidence, Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["dim"])),

      1088 +            ),

      1089 +            border_style=Style(color=CORTEX_THEME["dim"]),

      1090 +            box=box.ROUNDED,

      1091 +        ))

      1092 +

      1093 +

      1094  # =============================================================================

      1095  # ASI-STYLE PROMPTS

      1096  # =============================================================================

      400 +    def _show_contrastive_comparison(self, note: dict, diagnosis) -> None:

      401 +        """

      402 +        Show side-by-side comparison when discrimination error detected.

      403 +

      404 +        Uses the ConfusionMatrix to find the most confused concept pair

      405 +        and renders a contrastive panel.

      406 +        """

      407 +        try:

      408 +            from src.cortex.contrastive import get_contrastive_data

      409 +

      410 +            # Get the atom/concept that was confused

      411 +            atom_id = str(note.get("id", ""))

      412 +            if not atom_id:

      413 +                return

      414 +

      415 +            # Get the most confused pair from ConfusionMatrix

      416 +            if not hasattr(self.ncde, "confusion_matrix"):

      417 +                return

      418 +

      419 +            worst_pair = self.ncde.confusion_matrix.get_worst_pair(atom_id)

      420 +            if not worst_pair:

      421 +                return

      422 +

      423 +            confused_id, confusion_score = worst_pair

      424 +            if confusion_score < 0.3:  # Threshold for showing comparison

      425 +                return

      426 +

      427 +            # Fetch contrastive data

      428 +            concept_a, concept_b, evidence = get_contrastive_data(atom_id, confused_id)

      429 +

      430 +            # Render the comparison panel

      431 +            ui.render_contrastive_panel(

      432 +                console,

      433 +                concept_a=concept_a,

      434 +                concept_b=concept_b,

      435 +                confusion_evidence=evidence,

      436 +            )

      437 +

      438 +        except Exception as e:

      439 +            logger.debug(f"Could not show contrastive comparison: {e}")

      440 +

      502      def _check_answer_correct(self, response: str, session: SocraticSession) -> bool:

      503 -        """Check if learner's response contains the correct answer."""

      503 +        """

      504 +        Check if learner's response contains the correct answer.

      505 +

      506 +        Enhanced with:

      507 +        1. Numeric extraction ("192 is the answer" -> check for 192)

      508 +        2. Fuzzy matching for near-correct responses

      509 +        3. Pattern matching for answer declarations

      510 +        """

      511          back = session.atom_content.get("back", "")

      512          back_lower = back.lower()

      515 +        # 1. Extract and check numeric answers

      518 +            r"(\d+)\s*(?:is|equals?|gives?|=)\s*(?:the\s*)?(?:answer|result|it)",

      519 +            r"(?:so\s+)?(?:it'?s|the\s+answer\s+is|i\s+get)\s+(\d+)",

      523 +        ]

      524 +

      525 +        # Extract expected numeric from back

      526 +        expected_numbers = re.findall(r'\b(\d+)\b', back_lower)

      527 +

      528 +        for pattern in numeric_patterns:

      529 +            matches = re.findall(pattern, response_lower)

      530 +            if matches:

      531 +                # Flatten matches (some patterns have groups)

      532 +                found_numbers = []

      533 +                for m in matches:

      534 +                    if isinstance(m, tuple):

      535 +                        found_numbers.extend(m)

      536 +                    else:

      537 +                        found_numbers.append(m)

      538 +

      539 +                # Check if any found number matches expected

      540 +                for num in found_numbers:

      541 +                    if num in expected_numbers:

      542 +                        return True

      543 +

      544          # Handle JSON back (MCQ, etc.)

      545          try:

      546              back_data = json.loads(back)
